Here in the\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 296\n|PortionCalories = 37\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 8 - Makes one jar of [[Sun-dried tomatoes]]\n|Difficulty = 1\n|ImageComment = Oven-dried cherry tomatoes - done\n|TotalTime = 7 hours 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 7 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Sun-dried tomatoes at home 1.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Who knew you could do this?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">What a brilliant idea, and it works so well.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n==Sun-dried tomatoes, without the sun==\n\n[[Sun-dried tomatoes]] are a great item to have in the [[refrigerator]] as they have a long shelf-life and a small amount can lift almost any dish.\n\nHere in the UK we seem to get very little sun so we have to resort to other methods.\n\nMaking [[Sun-dried tomatoes]] without the sun is an ideal task for a slow Aga.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 16 large, good flavoured [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] or 32 cherry tomatoes\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Caster sugar|caster sugar]]\n| A few sprigs of [[Thyme|thyme]]\n| 500ml of [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| Sea [[Salt|salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to it's lowest setting. About 100\u00b0 C (225\u00b0 F - gas &frac14;), Aga: 'simmering oven'\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| With a sharp knife, cut the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] in half.\n| Lay them out on [[baking tray]]s, lined with greaseproof paper, sprinkle with sugar and drizzle them with a little [[Olive|olive]] [[Oil|oil]].\n| Pick the [[thyme]] leaves off and sprinkle over the [[tomatoes]], if you have lots of thyme you can lay the sprigs amongst the tomatoes for extra flavour.\n| Place them in the oven for about 7 hours, or until most of the moisture has been removed - check them every hour or so as you don't want them to be crispy!\n| Remove them and leave them to cool\n| Sprinkle a [[Sterilised|sterilised]] jar with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and add the sprigs of [[Thyme|thyme]].\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and cover with [[Olive|olive]] [[Oil|oil]].\n| They should keep for 6 months if refrigerated and always covered with [[Oil|oil]].\n}}\n===Variations===\n\nAdd a tablespoon of [[Chili|chili]] flakes if you like them spicy.\n\n==See also==\n* '''[[Oven-dried tomatoes]]\n===FOOD POISONING===\n\nDon't add [[Garlic|garlic]] as some recipes suggest because there is a '''very real danger of botulism''' as it is an anaerobic toxin (one that develops in an air-free environment - read: [[Talk:Garlic olive oil]].\n\nIf you want to be really scared, [http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Botulism read what Wikipedia has to say on botulism].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Dehydrated]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tomatoes #thyme #olive #bakingtray #sterilised #sundriedtomatorecipe #garlic #refrigerator #blackpepper #castersugar #dehydrated </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "The New official recipe for Spaghetti Bolognaise",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=The New official recipe for Spaghetti Bolognaise\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#spaghettibolognaise #officialSpagBol #officialRagu #2023ragu #bolognapasta #tomatopaste #tomatoes #broth #cookery #italian #ragu #revampedragu|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=The official recipe for bolognaise Pasta pasta sauce, which is one of the most famous Italian dishes, has been updated after 40 years.\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=24th April 2023\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour\n|CookTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 2778\n|PortionCalories = 463 \n|Image = [[Image:The New official recipe for Spaghetti Bolognaise recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">It's THE OFFICIAL RECIPE!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">How could I possibly not give it 5 stars \ud83e\udd13</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jeremy]] </span></span>\n}}\nThe '''official recipe''' for [[Bolognaise|bolognaise]] [[Pasta sauce|pasta sauce]], which is one of the most famous [[Italian]] dishes, has been updated after 40 years. The new recipe was created by a special committee from the Italian [[Cookery]] Academy and was deposited as a deed with The Chamber of Commerce in [[Bologna]]. This recipe replaces the original 1892 formula for [[Ragu|ragu]] alla bolognaise.\n\nThe new recipe removes [[Cream|cream]] and cartella, which is a [[Cut of beef|cut of beef]] that is hard to find nowadays. Good quality [[Stock cubes|stock cubes]] are now allowed. \"''Today we are consigning to our grandchildren something that is immortal. And we are teaching the culture of our city through a good plate of [[Tagliatelle|tagliatelle]]''\", said Valerio Veronesi, the president of [[Bologna]]'s Chamber of Commerce. \n\nRoberto Ariani, Secretary General of the [[Italian]] [[Cookery]] Academy, explained \"''In 40 years cookery has changed. What was accepted in the past may not be appreciated by contemporary   palates. That is why we have decided to modify the rag\u00f9 recipe.''\"\n\nThe earliest documented recipe for [[Ragu|ragu]] served with [[Pasta|pasta]] dates back to Imola, near [[Bologna]] in the late 18th century. The academy experts advise [[saut\u00e9ing]] the [[Minced meat|minced meat]] separately from the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and will allow chopped chicken livers and hearts. Smoked pancetta, [[Garlic|garlic]], and [[Herbs|herbs]] such as [[Rosemary|rosemary]] and [[Parsley|parsley]] are not allowed. [[Brandy]] and [[Flour|flour]] cannot be used for thickening the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n\nSome of the changes may offend traditionalists, and members of the academy acknowledge this. Atos Cavazza, a representative of the Academy's [[Bologna]] branch, noted: \"''This document is not intended to be the [[Sole|sole]] recipe but it is a recommendation to follow.''\"\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 400g coarsely [[Minced beef|minced beef]]\n| 150g chopped [[Pork|pork]] [[Pancetta|pancetta]]\n| Half an [[Onion|onion]]\n| 1 [[Carrot|carrot]]\n| 12 stick of [[Celery|celery]]\n| 1 [[Glass|glass]] of [[Red or white wine|red or white wine]]\n| 200g [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato paste|tomato paste]]\n| 1 [[Glass|glass]] of [[Whole milk|whole milk]]\n| light [[Meat|meat]] or [[Vegetable|vegetable]] [[Broth|broth]] ([[Stock cubes|stock cubes]] permitted)\n| 3 tablespoon [[Extra virgin Olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Begin by placing the [[Pancetta|pancetta]] in a [[Dutch Oven|dutch oven]] that is at room temperature, and then place it over medium heat.\n| Allow the pancetta to render its [[Fat|fat]] before adding the chopped [[Celery|celery]], [[Carrots|carrots]] and [[Onion|onion]], followed by a pinch of [[Salt|salt]]. \n| Let it soften for around 5 minutes before adding the [[Ground beef|ground beef]] that has been coarsely [[Ground|ground]], and break it apart in the pan.\n| [[Brown]] the [[Meat|meat]] well for approximately 5 minutes over high heat.\n| Once the [[Meat|meat]] is [[Browned|browned]], pour in the [[Wine|wine]] and allow it to reduce until the pan is almost [[Dry|dry]].\n| Pour in the [[Broth|broth]] and [[Passata|passata]] until the meat is fully covered. Reduce the heat to low and let it [[Simmer|simmer]] uncovered for approximately an hour.\n| After an hour has passed, add the [[MILK|milk]] and continue cooking over low heat for another hour. If it looks like the mixture is getting [[Dry|dry]], add more [[Broth|broth]] or water as necessary.\n| It's important to stir every 15 minutes or so throughout the cooking process.\n| After two hours have passed, turn off the heat and serve with [[Fresh pasta|fresh pasta]] such as [[Tagliatelle|tagliatelle]] or fettuccine made with [[Eggs|eggs]].\n}}\n\n\n===Recipe source===\n* The official recipe for [[Ragu|ragu]] served with [[Pasta|pasta]] or [[Bolognaise|bolognaise]] [[Pasta sauce|pasta sauce]] as defined by the committee of the [[Italian]] [[Cookery]] Academy, 2023\n===Chef's notes===\n[[Tomato puree]] and [[Tomato paste|tomato paste]] are both made from cooked, [[Strained|strained]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], but there are some differences between them.\n\n[[Tomato puree]] is a smooth and thick liquid that is made by cooking and straining fresh [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]. It has a bright red color and a relatively thin consistency, similar to that of a thick [[Soup|soup]]. It may have some seasonings or other [[Vegetables|vegetables]] added to it, but it does not usually have any added [[Sugar|sugar]]. [[Tomato]] [[Puree|puree]] is commonly used as a base for [[Sauces|sauces]], [[Soups|soups]], [[Stews|stews]], and other dishes.\n\n[[Tomato paste]], on the other [[Hand|hand]], is a thick and concentrated paste made by cooking down [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] for several hours to remove most of the water content. This results in a thick and dense paste that is very rich in tomato flavor. [[Tomato]] paste is darker in color than [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]] and has a much thicker consistency. It is often sold in small cans or tubes and is used to add intense tomato flavor to [[Sauces|sauces]], [[Soups|soups]], and [[Stews|stews]]. Some tomato paste brands may have added [[Sugar|sugar]] or [[Salt|salt]].\n\nIn summary, [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]] is a smooth and thin liquid made from cooked and [[Strained|strained]] fresh [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], while [[Tomato paste|tomato paste]] is a thick and concentrated paste made by cooking down tomatoes to remove most of the water content.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#spaghettibolognaise #officialSpagBol #officialRagu #2023ragu #bolognapasta #tomatopaste #tomatoes #broth #cookery #italian #ragu #revampedragu</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

scraped and finely [[Diced|diced]]\n| 2 [[Celery|celery]] sticks, finely [[Diced|diced]] (include the leaves is you have them)\n| 2 medium [[Red onions|red onions]], peeled and coarsely [[Diced|diced]]\n| 4 cloves of [[Garlic]], peeled and finely [[Diced|diced]], or to taste.\n| 150ml [[Red wine|red wine]] or [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 tbsp [[tomato pur\u00e9e]]\n| 40 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 3 [[Roast peppers|red peppers, roasted]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 2 x 400 g tins chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| seasoning\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 250g Thomas the Tank Engine [[Pasta|pasta]] shapes\n| 30g [[Parmesan cheese]], freshly [[Grated|grated]] (optional)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a deep saut\u00e9 or [[Frying pan|frying pan]] on a high heat.\n| When hot, but not [[Smoking|smoking]], add the [[Carrots|carrots]], [[Celery|celery]], [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]]. \n| Reduce the heat to medium and cook until the [[Onions|onions]] are soft.\n| Stir in the [[wine]] and [[tomato pur\u00e9e]] and allow to cook for 5 minutes, uncovered.\n| Add the [[Butter|butter]], [[Peppers|peppers]] and the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n| Cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] slowly for 1 hour.\n| Add the [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] gently for a further 30 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, [[Boil|boil]] up two kettles-full of water and pour into a large saucepan.\n| Once the water is [[Boiling|boiling]], add the [[Pasta|pasta]] shapes and cook for 7-8 minutes. \n| When the [[Pasta|pasta]] is cooked, drain and  plate immediately.\n| Cover with the [[Sauce|sauce]] and serve, sprinkled with [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan]] if desired.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Thomas the Tank Engine Pasta individual shapes.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Thomas the Tank Engine [[Pasta]] individual shapes\nImage:Thomas the Tank Engine Pasta.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Thomas the Tank Engine [[Pasta]]\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Italian]] [[Bread|bread]] and side [[Salad|salad]].\n===Variations===\nIf you are are cooking for young children, use [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]] instead of [[Wine|wine]] and a mild [[Cheese|cheese]] instead of the [[Parmesan]].  Adults, add some [[chillies]] or [[chilli powder]] to give the sauce a kick!\n===Chef's notes===\nFor a change, I am blending the sauce until smooth - a good way of disguising [[vegetables]] for reluctant children.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pasta]]\n[[Category:British recipes|Pasta]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes|Pasta]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pasta]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Pasta]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Pasta]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Pasta]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine|Pasta]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pasta #diced #thomasthetankenginepastaintomatosauce #tomatoes #carrots #grated #simmer #butter #onions #wine #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It's fairly heavy on the calories, though you could use [[single cream]] to reduce them a little!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 16 sponge fingers (savoiardi)\n| 150 ml (5 oz) [[double cream]]\n| 250 g (9 oz) [[mascarpone cream]]\n| 200 ml strong espresso coffee at room temperature\n| 1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n| 3 tablespoons [[rum]] - [[brandy]] or [[Tia Maria]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[icing sugar]]\n| Coco powder (ideally in a shaker)\n| [[Sprig of mint]] to garnish\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Whip the [[cream]] and 3 tablespoons [[icing sugar]] until well mixed\n| Beat in the [[mascarpone]], 1 tablespoon of the rum (or [[brandy]] or Tia maria) and the [[vanilla]] extract\n| Mix the remaining [[sugar]] and [[rum]] (or [[brandy]] or [[Tia maria]]) into the coffee\n| You can either make this directly into serving glasses or make in one dish (which is probably better for the waistline)\n| Dip 4 fingers in the coffee and line the bottom of the dish (or 4 serving glasses)\n| Add a layer of [[mascarpone]] mixture, a layer of soaked sponge fingers and so on\n| Finish with a layer of [[mascarpone]]\n| Pour any remaining coffee mixture over the top and dust with coco powder \n| Chill for 30 minutes before serving\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nGarnish with [[mint leaves]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tiramisu #brandy #mascarpone #icingsugar #rum #tiamaria #mascarponecream #singlecream #sprigofmint #mintleaves #doublecream </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Its a great idea for a starting point for many..\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=2nd August 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 3\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 30 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 1832\n|PortionCalories = 610\n|Image = [[Image:Tomato and cheese macaroni tray bake recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">That's colourful!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Looked so good, I didn't want to spoil it by eating it!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is very loosely based on one of the tomato recipes in Jamie Oliver's ''Jamie's Kitchen'', (I think).\n[[Image:MacaroniBake ready for the oven.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready to bake for 30 minutes]]\n\nIt's a great idea for a starting point for many recipes and a very good way to use up your glut of home-grown [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 135g [[Dried|dried]] [[Macaroni|macaroni]], cooked [[Al-dente|al-dente]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| A pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]] chopped finely\n| 100g cooking [[Pancetta|pancetta]], cube\n| 3 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 6 large [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 12 small [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| &#189; a teaspoon of [[Dried|dried]] [[Dill|dill]]\n| 10 fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]]\n| 1 ball [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Chilli oil|chilli oil]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Cook the [[Pasta|pasta]] for 7-9 minutes in fast [[Boiling|boiling]] [[Salted|salted]] water.  Drain well.\n* Pre-heat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| [[Saute]] the chopped [[Onion|onion]] in a tablespoon of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] for 3 minutes.\n| Stir in the cubed [[Pancetta|pancetta]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] so it takes a tiny bit of colour.\n| Add the [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]] and cook for a minute, stirring while it cooks.\n| Pour this mixture into a smallish [[Baking tray|baking tray]] and move it around so it coats the base with the [[Oil|oil]].\n| Halve the small [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and quarter the large tomatoes and add them to the tray with the [[Macaroni|macaroni]] and [[Dried|dried]] [[Dill|dill]].\n| Chop the [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], reserve half for garnish and add the [[Rest|rest]] to the mixture.  Stir well to combine.\n| [[Crumble]] the ball of [[Mozzarella|mozzarella]] over the top and drizzle with the remaining [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Chilli oil|chilli oil]].\n| [[Bake]] at the top of a  180\u00b0 C [[Oven|oven]] for 30 minutes or until the [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]] starts to crust.\n| Garnish with the remaining chopped basil.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis is nice served with crusty [[Bread|bread]] and would probably stretch to four people if served this way.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tomatoes #dried #oliveoil #mozzarellacheese #pancetta #dill #tomatoandcheesemacaronitraybake #basilleaves #macaroni #onion #chillioil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Be generous with the olive oil!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1395\n|PortionCalories = 139\n|DatePublished=8th April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Servings: 10 - 1 large loaf\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  45 minutes + resting time\n|PrepTime = 20 minutes + resting time \n|CookTime =  25 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tomato and olive focaccia TM recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Finally, Focaccia..</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..that can be made in my Thermy</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\nI love [[Focaccia|focaccia]] and this is one more recipe, which I personally think is one of the best.  Be generous with the [[olive oil]]!\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n\n| 300g [[Sparkling mineral water|sparkling mineral water]]\n| 500g stong [[White bread|white bread]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| 7g fast action [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| [[Extra virgin olive oil]]\n| 1-2 [[tomatoes]] (depending on size), chopped or a few cherry [[tomatoes]], cut in half\n| 2 tsps [[dried oregano]]\n| Green or black [[olives]], cut in half if large\n| [[Coarse salt]] (sea or Himalayan [[Rock|rock]])\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the water and the [[Flour|flour]] to the bowl '''30 sec / Speed 5'''.\n| Leave for 1 hour to autolyse.\n| Add the [[Yeast|yeast]] and [[Salt|salt]] to separate sides of the bowl '''10 seconds / Speed 7'''.\n| Then '''2 minutes / [[Knead]]'''.\n| Remove the [[Dough|dough]] from the bowl and form a ball.\n| Place the [[Dough|dough]] into a bowl and pour [[Olive oil|olive oil]] over the [[Dough|dough]] to make sure it is well coated.\n| Cover and leave to [[Rest|rest]] overnight in the [[Fridge|fridge]].\n| The next day, remove from the [[Fridge|fridge]] and bring to room temperature.\n| Pour enough [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to cover the base of a [[Roasting|roasting]] pan about 20 x 30cm.\n| Put the [[Dough|dough]] in the centre of the pan and let it [[Rest|rest]], covered, for 30 minutes.\n| Turn the [[Dough|dough]] in the [[Oil|oil]] (it must be nice and oily) and spread it with the tip of your fingers from the centre.\n| Sprinkle with [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] pieces or [[Cherry tomatoes|cherry tomatoes]], cut in half and push well into the [[Dough|dough]] with the [[Olives|olives]]. \n| Sprinkle with [[Oregano|oregano]], [[salt]] and more [[Oil|oil]].\n| Allow to [[Rest|rest]] until doubled in size.\n| Cook on the bottom rack of a preheated [[Oven|oven]] for 25 minutes at 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 180\u00b0 C]\n| Allow to cool on a wire rack.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nLovely on its own or with [[Salads|salads]].\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Translated and adapted from a recipe by '''[http://www.ricette-bimby.com/2010/07/focaccia-barese-col-bimby.html Ricette Bimby]''' under '''[http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/ CC BY-NC-SA 3.0]'''\n===Variations===\nUse [[Sun-dried tomatoes|sun-dried tomatoes]] if preferred.\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes|Focaccia tomato olive]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dough #rest #oliveoil #tomatoes #olives #flour #focaccia #fridge #favouriterecipesfocacciatomatoolive #whitebread #yeast </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tomato sauce for pizza",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tomato sauce for pizza, Italian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tomatosauceforpizza #slowcooker #garlic #tomatopuree #sherryvinegar #parmesancheese #tomatoes #pizzas #chilipowder #simmer #redwine \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=If you are making your own pizzas, then you'll need this recipe for a spicy topping. Make larger quantities and freeze the remainders for the next\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 305\n|PortionCalories = 38\n|DatePublished=3rd October 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Servings: 8 - Enough for four large [[pizzas]]\n|Difficulty = 2\n|ImageComment = Blitzed and reduced\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Tomato sauce reduced.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I use this once a week</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">One of my favourite recipes.  We make 6 times this amount at one time and freeze the remains in plastic cups for making pizzas.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nIf you are making your own [[pizzas]], then you'll need this recipe for a spicy topping.\n\nWe find this recipe so good, I make large batches and freeze in plastic coffee cups and [[vacuum-seal]] for later use.  Half a plastic cup is enough for 2 large pizzas. \n\nThere is a good basic [[pizza dough|pizza dough recipe here]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 30 ml [[olive oil]]\n| 1 [[onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, crushed\n| &#189; teaspoon [[chili pepper]] flakes\n| Pinch [[chili powder]]\n| 90 ml [[red wine]]\n| Dash of [[sherry vinegar]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[tomato puree]]\n| 1 x 400 g can peeled [[plum tomatoes]], chopped\n| Big handful [[basil leaves]], torn\n| 2 teaspoons [[dried]] [[oregano]]\n| sprig fresh [[thyme leaves]],\n| 1 teaspoon [[demerara sugar]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Parmesan cheese]], freshly [[grated]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Tomato sauce for pizza recipe.jpg|Tomato sauce for pizza\nImage:Tomato sauce for pizza slow cooker.jpg|Reducing in a [[slow cooker]]\nImage:Frozen pizza topping.jpg|Frozen in batches, enough here for 20 large pizzas!\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[oil]] in a pan and add the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[chili flakes]], [[chili powder]] and [[onions]] and [[fry]] gently until translucent, about 4 minutes\n| Add the [[paprika powder]], [[red wine]] and [[sherry vinegar]] and [[simmer]] to reduce by half\n| Add the chopped [[tomatoes]] to the pan with the [[tomato puree]] and bring to the [[boil]]\n| Add the remaining [[herbs]], reduce and [[simmer]] for 30 minutes\n| Pour the sauce into a [[food processor]] with a blade and blitz to a puree\n| ''or'', if you have a [[stick blender]], a few minutes with that will have the same effect, ideal if you're using a [[slow cooker]].  \n| Return to the pan and add the [[sugar]] and [[Parmesan cheese]] and cook for a further 15 minutes\n| Season with [[salt]] and [[pepper]], the final consistency should be a paste not runny.  Reduce a little more if required.\n| Allow to cool\n}}\n===Chef's tip===\nRecently I made a huge batch of pizza topping with this years' surplus [[tomatoes]] with the intention to [[vacuum pack]] them into single [[pizza]] portions. I used the basic procedure as above, but for the reducing stage, added the sauce to a [[slow cooker]] on high to 12 hours, uncovered (or until the sauce reaches a nice thick consistency).  The sauce was then frozen into about half full paper coffee and then [[vacuum packed]].  An absolute success.   \n\nIf you are making the sauce ahead of the pizzas and it needs further reduction, just remove from the heat and leave to dry  out a little, naturally.  This works especially well in a large frying pan.\n\nA brilliant, but rather obvious idea that has only come to me recently, is to make double the amount, bag it up and freeze it in one or two pizza portions.  Home made pizzas are great, but sometimes it's too much hassle to have to make the sauce as well.\n\nBottled bolognese type sauce makes a good very pizza topping with very little effort. Freeze the remainder in pizza portion sized bags for the next pizza making session.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tomatosauceforpizza #slowcooker #garlic #tomatopuree #sherryvinegar #parmesancheese #tomatoes #pizzas #chilipowder #simmer #redwine </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

[[Chicken]] would work just as well.  Do ensure that the meat is properly cooked.  If you want to use uncooked [[chicken]] or [[turkey]], use [[Steamed chicken|this recipe]] to prepare it first.\n[[Image:Turkey pizza.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Turkey pizza ready to slide on to the [[pizza stone]]]]\n\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 portion of [[Pizza dough]] - Makes 2 pizzas\n| 2 balls of [[mozzarella cheese]]\n| 200g cooked [[Chicken|chicken]] or [[Turkey|turkey]]\n| &#189; bottle of [[Dolmio tomato and garlic pasta sauce]], or make your own [[Tomato sauce for pizza|pizza sauce]]\n| A few slices of raw [[Onion|onion]]\n| Slices of fresh [[green chillies]] (optional)\n| 30g grated [[cheddar cheese]] (optional)\n| 15ml olive oil\n| [[Fine yellow cornmeal]] for dusting\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Make the [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] as instructed\n* If using a [[pizza stone]], preheat the [[pizza stone]] under a very hot [[grill]] for about 20 minutes.  Place it about 8cm (3\") from the heat source.\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Make 1 pizza per person\n| Sprinkle the worksurface with [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]]\n| Stretch or roll the [[Dough|dough]] into two thin rounds\n| Prick the pizzas all over with a fork. This prevents it puffing up too much and burning while it is cooking\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] one side of the [[Pizza|pizza]] and [[Grill|grill]], oiled side down for about 3 minutes or until it starts to brown and puff up.\n| Remove from the oven, flip over and add the topping.\n| Drizzle the [[Pizza|pizza]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and spread the pizza with &frac12; of the [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]]\n| Lay a few slices of the raw onion on the tomato topping.\n| Add the chopped turkey \n| Top with torn [[Mozzarella|mozzarella]] and a drizzle of [[olive oil]].\n| [[Bake]] for 3 or 4  minutes or until the [[Cheese|cheese]] browns a little - watch it carefully as it can burn easily.\n| Keep the fist pizza warm at the bottom of the oven whilst you make the second.\n| Serve hot\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nPasta sauce such as the 350 g Dolmio range makes a perfect pizza topping.  The unused half can be put straight in the freezer ready for the next two pizzas!\n\nIf you don't have a [[pizza stone]] you can lay the pizza on a [[grill tray]] instead, it just won't be quite as good.\n\n''I trust [[User:PaoloCastagna|Paolo]] won't be too upset that I have included this in the [[Italian recipes]] section.''\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#turkeypizza #pizzastone #chicken #turkey #oliveoil #pizza #pizzadough #grill #mozzarella #bake #onion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This is my adapted, vegetarian version of Elizabeth David's recipe from Italian Food\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2414\n|PortionCalories = 402\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 14 hours 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours\n |CookTime = 2 hours 35 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Zuppa di minestrone recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Perrfection</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Better than anything from a tin</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nProbably [[Italy]]'s most famous [[Soup|soup]].  This is my adapted, [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] version of Elizabeth David's recipe from ''Italian Food'' (ISBN 0140460985).\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 2 [[Onions|onions]], finely chopped\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, chopped\n| 1 tablespoon fresh or 1 teaspoon each of [[Dried thyme|dried thyme]] and [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 4 [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped or if not in season, 1 x 400g tin of [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], drained\n| 125ml [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| 110g [[Cannellini beans|cannellini beans]], soaked overnight\n| 1.75 [[Litres|litres]] [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 2 [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and [[Diced|diced]] - about 200g after trimming and peeling\n| 2 small waxy [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and [[Diced|diced]] - about 125g after trimming and peeling\n| 1 small [[Turnip|turnip]], peeled and [[Diced|diced]] - about 100g after trimming and peeling\n| 90g [[French beans]], trimmed and cut in half\n| 1 stick [[Celery|celery]], chopped\n| &frac12; small [[Cabbage|cabbage]] (or a whole sweetheart [[cabbage]], [[Shredded|shredded]]\n| 50g [[Orzo|orzo]], or other small [[Pasta|pasta]] shapes\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Parmesan cheese]]\n| Seasoning\n| Extra [[Parmesan cheese]] for serving\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a deep pan and gently saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Herbs|herbs]].\n| Stir in the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Red wine|red wine]] and allow to [[Bubble|bubble]] for a couple of minutes.\n| Add the drained [[Cannellini beans|cannellini beans]] and the [[Stock|stock]] and [[Boil|boil]] gently (covered) for 2 hours.\n| Add the [[Carrots|carrots]], and 15 minutes later, uncover, and add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and [[Turnip|turnip]].\n| 10 minutes later, add the [[French beans]], [[Celery|celery]], [[Cabbage|cabbage]] and [[Orzo|orzo]].\n| After a further 10 minutes, stir in the [[Parmesan]] and check seasoning.\n| Serve more [[Parmesan]] separately.\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse haricot or other [[White beans|white beans]] and you can vary the [[Vegetables|vegetables]].  Some [[Italian]] sources say that little or no [[Tomato|tomato]] should be included, so you can leave them out if desired.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#zuppadiminestrone #diced #cabbage #garlic #orzo #celery #parmesan #frenchbeans #turnip #parmesancheese #cannellinibeans </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
